Rickshaw Rental: Calculation of Both Big and Small Dollars 107

Regarding the payment of rickshaw rental by public rickshaw pullers, the Rickshaw Affairs Committee has issued a notice and posted it at rickshaw inspection stations, license registration offices, and various branches of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association, advising rickshaw pullers to pay in large dollars to avoid exploitation and loss by rickshaw owners. The Rickshaw Affairs Committee has previously posted a notice, displayed at rickshaw inspection, licensing, and mutual aid offices, that all payments should be made in big dollars in order to avoid exploitation and loss. The rickshaw rental fee (including the mutual aid fee) has long been stipulated by the Municipal Council. The maximum rate is 85 cents per day. Traditionally, there are two shifts, morning and evening, which vary in length. If the morning and evening shifts are of equal length, then the rental fee will also be the same, with a maximum of 42.5 cents per shift. According to current market prices, this amount is equivalent to 50 cents in small dollars and three copper coins, or two dimes and 28 copper coins. It is hoped that all rickshaw pullers will be informed and calculate accordingly.

Industrial Expert Huang Xiancheng Invents a Travel Folding Cabinet 115

Currently Applying to the Ministry for a Patent

Mr. Huang Xiancheng is from Changsha, Hunan Province. He studied at Beijing Normal University. In the ninth year of the Republic [1920], he went to France at his own expense and was admitted to the Paris Higher Industrial School. He then transferred to the Belgian National Industrial School to study machinery. He completed his studies and returned to China in the seventeenth year of the Republic [1928]. He successively served as an engineer and mechanical instructor at the Military Transportation Research Institute of the Chinese Industrial Arts School. Recently, he has used his years of knowledge to invent a type of travel folding cabinet. Last year, he applied to the Ministry of Industry for a patent. Unexpectedly, the Ministry misunderstood, thinking it was for ordinary travel use, and did not approve it. Mr. Huang personally took the structure of the cabinet, its benefits, to the Academia Sinica, requesting experimentation. The president of the academy, Cai Yuanpei, consulted with many people and confirmed it as a new invention in industry. Besides writing a letter to the Ministry of Industry to prove it for Mr. Huang, he also wrote a written introduction. The content roughly stated: “Mr. Huang Xiancheng has created the Xiancheng travel cabinet. Its structure is divided into three types, and each type can be deduced and changed into ten or a hundred types, with minor differences. The novel and exquisite cabinet is about one and a half meters high, one meter wide, and half a meter deep. It can be opened, closed, or folded at any time. Inside, there is a clothes rod for hanging Chinese and Western clothes, as well as arbitrarily spaced partitions for placing books, and a document bag for placing small items. It is truly an original creation, different from those that are imitated or modified. The design began during the January 28th Truce [1932] and went through a long period of painstaking research and repeated improvements, finally succeeding in the spring of the twenty-third year [1934]. The difficulty of the creation can be seen from this. The reason it is named a travel cabinet is because in recent times, transportation is convenient, and there are many people traveling, as well as male and female students studying far away. Whenever they arrive at a place, they always need a wardrobe. If they buy one everywhere, the cost is not small, and it is heavy and difficult to move. If they don't buy one, clothes are easily soiled, which is very inconvenient. Moreover, bookshelves cannot be dispensed with, so he created an item that serves as both a wardrobe and a bookshelf. It is sturdy, lightweight, and convenient for travel and carrying. When not traveling, it can be used as furniture, saving money and being most suitable for the middle class. In addition, it can also be decorated with brocade and embroidery, making it suitable for wealthy families. Its structure is exquisite, and when it is released to the world in the future, it will surely become very popular.” Currently, Mr. Huang has resubmitted the application to the Ministry of Industry for a patent based on the points proven by Mr. Cai, and it is expected that there will be no problems and that it will be approved soon.

The Integrated Compilation of County and District Administrative Regulations, published by the Datong Bookstore, is now available for pre-order. The content of this book is extremely rich, including over two hundred types of regulations related to county and district administration, totaling over six hundred thousand words. It is divided into ten sections: "Legal Sources," "Organizational Law," "Official Regulations," "Civil Affairs," "Police," "Autonomy," "Finance," "Education," "Industry," and "Land." All regulations promulgated and implemented by the central government are included, and important old regulations that continue to be valid are also selectively included. If there are ambiguities in the articles that have been officially interpreted by the government, the main points are extracted and placed after. All laws and plans related to county and district administration are also included, which can be used as a reference for administrative implementation and as a consultant for daily office work. Those working in county governments or district offices should each have a copy. The entire book is six volumes and is priced at five yuan. During the pre-order period, it is only two yuan.

Autopsy Report of Ge Gongzhen (Continued) 123

(B) Microscopic Examination: (1) Peritoneum: On the peritoneal surface of the peritoneum, there are deposits of fibrinous and polymorphonuclear leukocyte exudates. The mesothelial cells on the membrane surface are necrotic and adhere to the exudates on the surface. Here, the peritoneal tissue shows polymorphonuclear leukocyte cell infiltration, blood vessel dilation, and acute inflammatory changes. (2) Intestine: The mucosa and submucosa of the small and large intestines do not show lesions. The outer layer of the muscle layer and the subserosal layer show significant polymorphonuclear cell and a small number of mononuclear wandering cell infiltration, congestion, and edema. On the peritoneal surface, there are deposits of fibrinous and leukocytic exudates. (3) Mesenteric and retroperitoneal lymph nodes: The peritoneal surface of the mesentery has a small amount of fibrin and leukocytic exudates deposited. The mesenteric lymph nodes do not show inflammatory changes. The retroperitoneal lymph nodes are hyperplastic, with an excessive number of polymorphonuclear leukocytes and mononuclear cells accumulated in them. The blood vessels are dilated. (4) Bladder: The peritoneum is normal. The subserosal layer shows slight cell infiltration, mostly small round cells and mononuclear cells. The muscle layer also shows the same type of infiltration, with the addition of polymorphonuclear cells. The outer layer of the bladder wall shows significant polymorphonuclear cell infiltration, and fibrinous exudates are also deposited on its membrane surface. (5) Prostate: The glandular follicles are mostly dilated and contain eosinophilic amorphous matter. In several places, the interstitium shows moderate small round cell, mononuclear cell, and polymorphonuclear leukocyte infiltration. (6) Kidney: Most glomeruli are normal, but a small number show fibrosis. Here, the interstitium also shows moderate or mild small round cell infiltration. The epithelial cells of the renal tubules show parenchymal degeneration, otherwise normal. In one place, a cyst is formed, with a very thin wall, and the inner membrane is covered with a single layer of flat cells. The cavity contains a small amount of eosinophilic substance. The wall of the renal pelvis is normal. (7) The outer capsule of the liver is nodular and shows polymorphonuclear leukocytes and fibrinous exudates deposited on its peritoneum. The liver substance shows multiple uneven and irregular hepatocyte masses, with a large amount of fibrous tissue interspersed. There is small round cell and mononuclear cell infiltration, and there are excessive bile capillaries. Therefore, the normal lobular structure of the liver is completely absent. In several places, multiple irregular dilated blood vessels and blood sinuses are accumulated into sheets, undoubtedly sponge-like hemangiomas. (8) Spleen: The outer membrane of the spleen also has fibrinous and leukocytic exudates. The number of lymphocytes is relatively small, but the size and cells are normal. The splenic pulp shows multiple erythrocytes and excessive polymorphonuclear leukocytes. Where congestion is not very obvious, the walls of the splenic pulp's blood vessels can be seen to be thickened. (9) Lung: The lung substance taken from the left lung shows fibrous degeneration, with calcareous caseous masses of varying sizes, around which a small number of multinucleated giant cells can be seen. The lung substance in other parts does not show lesions. (10) Stomach: The gastric mucosa is mostly normal, but in one place, there is an ulcer. This ulcer reaches the upper part of the muscle layer. The surface of the ulcer has a small amount of necrotic tissue deposited. In the tissue around the ulcer, the submucosa is the most obvious, showing moderate small round cell and mononuclear cell infiltration and increased fibrous tissue. The penis is slightly changed, and the axillary lymph nodes are not enlarged. (11) Aorta: The inner layer of the aorta shows local thickening, with increased fibrous cells and fatty substances. The middle and outer layers are normal. (12) Sphenoid sinus: The epithelium taken from the sphenoid sinus shows a normal epithelial layer. The subepithelial layer is slightly thicker than normal and has a small number of small round cells and mononuclear cells infiltrated. (13) Middle ear and other cervical spine bodies: Examination not completed. (14) Heart, gallbladder, thyroid, pituitary, pancreas, adrenal gland, thymus, testicle, and epididymis: Do not show significant lesions. (C) Bacteriological Report: According to the bacteriological report, hemolytic streptococci were detected by culture from abdominal fluid, pericardial fluid, urine, pus around the ureter, and heart blood. Escherichia coli was detected from abdominal fluid, urine, pus around the ureter, and pericardial fluid. Bile did not grow anything. (D) Parasitological Report: According to the parasitological report, stool was brown-red, with leukocytes 10, erythrocytes 10, mucus 10, and no parasites or eggs detected. (E) Diagnosis: Hemolytic streptococcal sepsis, complete acute membrane inflammation (hemolytic streptococcus), acute retroperitoneal cellulitis (hemolytic streptococcus), acute periureteritis (hemolytic streptococcus), acute retroperitoneal lymphadenitis, acute splenomegaly, parenchymal degeneration of internal organs, subacute cystitis (hemolytic streptococcus), subacute prostatitis, chronic sphenoid sinusitis, Ma's laceration of the abdominal wall, lack of appendix, mild ulcerative colitis, nodular cirrhosis, splenomegaly, chronic gastric ulcer, local chronic nephritis, chronic pulmonary tuberculosis, local pleural adhesions in the upper left, mild aortic sclerosis, cavernous hemangioma of the liver, congenital renal cyst, congenital phimosis on the right, congenital duodenal malformation.

(F) Surgical Pathology Report

(No. 3991) (A) Gross Examination: The examination material is an appendix, 4 cm long and 0.6 cm in diameter. Its outer membrane is smooth and shiny, but in several places, there are thin layers of yellow fibrinous exudates deposited. The blood vessels of the outer membrane are congested and tortuous. When cut open, the cut surface does not show obvious lesions. (B) Microscopic Examination: The appendix lumen does not contain exudates. The mucosa and submucosa are normal, but in the latter layer, there are several places with brown pigment deposits. The muscle layer has no lesions. The outer layer is edematous, the blood vessels are dilated, and there is moderate polymorphonuclear leukocyte and mononuclear cell infiltration. The outer membrane surface has a small amount of fibrinous and leukocytic exudates covering it. (C) Diagnosis: Acute periappendicitis. (G) Conclusion

According to the above sections, the cause of death was hemolytic streptococcal sepsis and complete acute peritonitis. The cause of the disease may have originated from sphenoid sinusitis. The patient must have had symptoms of hemolytic streptococcal influenza in the early stages. Later, the bacteria reached the sphenoid sinus from the nose, first causing acute sphenoid sinusitis, and then gradually turning into chronic sphenoid sinusitis. If the patient's resistance is strong, there will be no other complications. Otherwise, the bacteria will spread to other places, and other concurrent or secondary diseases will occur. In Ge's case, it may be because of overwork or fatigue on the road, leading to reduced resistance. Therefore, bacteria from the sphenoid sinus spread to the bladder, causing cystitis. The tissue around the bladder should have lymphatics, which are connected to the lymphatics of the retroperitoneal tissue. Therefore, the spread of cystitis outward can reach the retroperitoneal part, leading to acute retroperitoneal cellulitis. The accumulation of pus around the ureter that we found is also a manifestation of this disease. The pus accumulation area outside the right ureter is very close to the appendix, so it is clear that the symptoms of appendicitis can occur. The result of the appendix examination is a manifestation of complete acute peritonitis. The infection of the peritoneum can come from the retroperitoneal tissue or from blood transmission. In short, Ge's cause of death was various diseases caused by highly toxic hemolytic streptococcus. The most important of these were sepsis and complete acute peritonitis. Other symptoms such as pulmonary tuberculosis, cirrhosis, and gastric ulcer cannot be fatal. Reporter: Ai Shiguang, Associate Professor of Pathology, National Shanghai Medical College, November 3, 1935.

Methods for Raising Funds for Compulsory Education in Provinces, Cities, and Counties 125

Jointly drafted by the Ministries of Education and Finance, approved by the Executive Yuan for implementation

The Ministry of Education recently, together with the Ministry of Finance, drafted an outline of temporary measures for provinces, cities, and counties to raise funds for compulsory education. It was submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and approval and has now been approved and filed by the Executive Yuan. The Yuan has issued a circular to the provincial and municipal governments for implementation. The original text of the Executive Yuan's circular and the said measures are recorded below:

The Executive Yuan instructed the provincial and municipal governments, stating in brief: "Regarding the joint submission by the Ministries of Finance and Education on October 23 of this year, 'Regarding the joint telegraphic request submitted by the Director of the Education Department of Hunan Province and twenty-three directors of education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities such as Zhejiang and Shanghai to the Ministry of Education, requesting that it be forwarded to the Executive Yuan to issue a circular to the provincial and municipal governments, ordering the counties and cities to comply. The plans proposed by the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities stipulate that the compulsory education expenses that should be paid by the counties and cities each year should be allocated by the counties and cities as much as possible. The finance departments and bureaus of the provinces and cities should be instructed to do their best to plan for increasing education funds and should not use the excuse of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies to obstruct them.' After investigation by our departments, China has a vast territory, and there are many children who are out of school. It is indeed impossible for the expenses of compulsory education to be entirely covered by the national treasury or the treasuries of the provinces and cities. However, there should be special regulations and measures from the central government for the local governments to raise compulsory education funds on their own to serve as standards and avoid disputes. Now, our departments, based on Article 6 of the Outline of Temporary Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education, 'The principle of compulsory education funding is that the local governments are responsible for it,' and Article 25 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Outline of Temporary Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education, 'The compulsory education funds for a county or city should be allocated according to the local situation, or designated school properties, or designated special tax revenues, and the people may be encouraged to make donations to the best of their ability,' and with reference to the Financial Revenue and Expenditure System Law, have jointly drafted Temporary Measures for Provinces, Counties, and Cities to Raise Funds for Compulsory Education, so that there is something to follow when raising funds for compulsory education in various places. Whether this is appropriate or not, we have compiled these measures and attached a copy of the original telegraphic request to be submitted to your Yuan for review and filing, and we request that these temporary measures be circulated to the provincial and municipal governments for compliance.'"

Outline of Temporary Measures for Provinces, Counties, and Cities to Raise Funds for Compulsory Education

(1) This outline of measures is formulated based on Article 6 of the Outline of Temporary Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education and the provisions of Chapter 6 of the Detailed Rules for Implementation.

(2) The compulsory education funds in each elementary school district in each province, county, and city should be determined based on the number of schools established and the amount of funds needed. As a principle, more than half of the funds should be raised locally by each county and city.

(3) The compulsory education funds in each elementary school district in each province, county, and city should be verified and included in the county and city budgets by the county and city education administrative agencies. If there are increases after the budget is announced, they should be supplemented according to the procedures for supplementary budgets and be subject to the management and supervision of the local financial agencies.

(4) The revenue and expenditure of compulsory education funds in each elementary school district in each province, county, and city must be absolutely open and should be announced in the elementary school district at the end of each semester so that everyone knows.

(5) Provinces, counties, and cities should raise funds for compulsory education within the following scope: 1. Income from school properties designated by the provincial government upon approval by the county or city government. 2. Income from legal taxes and surtaxes designated by the provincial government upon approval by the county or city government. 3. Income from the reorganization of existing school properties in the counties, cities, townships, or school districts by the county or city government, resulting in increased revenue. 4. Voluntary donations to compulsory education funds by benevolent individuals. 5. Donations shared by the people in counties, cities, or townships through voluntary public consultation and approved according to law.

(6) The income from newly added compulsory education funds in the provinces, counties, cities, and townships, whose source is of a county-wide or city-wide nature, should be planned and allocated on a county-wide or city-wide basis. Those belonging to a township or a school district should be used for that township or school district immediately.

(7) The measures for raising compulsory education funds in municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan shall apply mutatis mutandis to the provisions of this outline regarding provinces or cities.

(8) These measures shall be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation.

Beijing Decides on Styles of Uniforms for Male and Female Students 126

And requests the Ministry of Education to order all middle schools in the country to wear them uniformly

(Nanjing, 9th dispatch) The Beijing Municipal Student Uniform Discussion Committee has decided on the styles of uniforms for all students in the city and has set a deadline for implementation starting from the 10th of next month. It has also requested the Ministry of Education to order all middle schools in the country to wear them uniformly. Elementary school boys will wear white in the summer, and short pants must reveal the knees. Girls will wear white tops (which may be changed to blue in the spring and autumn seasons) and black skirts. In winter, boys will follow the summer style but in black, with trousers lengthened, such as foreign black, following the styles set by the ministry. In winter, girls will wear blue long gowns.

The Ministry of Education Reissues a Circular to All Specialized Schools Urging Them to Quickly Organize Vocational Introduction Agencies 127

(Nanjing, 9th dispatch) The Ministry of Education has issued an order to all schools above the level of specialized colleges and universities nationwide to establish vocational introduction agencies and to cooperate closely with the National Academic Advisory Council. Currently, more than 30 schools, including National Peking University, have established introduction agencies and have sent letters informing the Advisory Council. The remaining 70 colleges and universities, including National Central University, have not sent letters reporting their establishment. The Advisory Council has submitted a request to the Ministry of Education to issue a circular to all these schools, ordering them to comply with the previous order and to establish vocational introduction agencies within a short period of time. The Ministry of Education reissued a circular on the 9th to all schools that have not yet organized, urging them to earnestly comply with the order to organize.

Xinjiang Youths Studying in Beijing Arrived in Beijing Last Night 129

The Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government held banquets to welcome them, and more than 20 organizations also hosted a tea party at Snow Garden.

The second group of twenty-one Xinjiang youth students arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. The Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government held banquets at Chunhua Restaurant yesterday to welcome them. More than twenty organizations from agriculture, industry, commerce, education, and other fields also hosted a tea party at Snow Garden. The situation was quite enthusiastic. The group of students left by train for Beijing last night. Details of the various events are summarized as follows:

Visiting the Municipal Government

After arriving in Shanghai, the Xinjiang students stayed at Wanzhu Elementary School. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, the Municipal Education Bureau specially provided cars and sent Lu Hailan, Yuan Zengyu, Ding Shoutang, and others to lead them to the central district of the city, the Municipal Government, the Education, Social Affairs, Health, Public Works, and Public Utilities Bureaus, as well as the Municipal Stadium, Library, and Museum, and other institutions. At noon, the Municipal Party Headquarters hosted a banquet at Chunhua Restaurant. In the afternoon, they visited Jiaotong University. Due to time constraints, the originally planned visits to various newspapers, bookstores, and factories were canceled. At 4:00 PM, various organizations hosted a reception at Snow Garden. In the evening, the Municipal Government hosted a banquet at Chunhua Restaurant. At 9:00 PM, they left Shanghai for Beijing.

Welcoming Xinjiang Youths Studying in Beijing (Photo by Wang Kai)

Party and Government Banquet

Yesterday at 12:00 noon, the Municipal Party Headquarters held a banquet at Chunhua Restaurant. Tong Xingbai and Jiang Huaisu from the Party Headquarters, Zhang Binghui from the Social Affairs Bureau, Lu Hailan, Yuan Zengyu, and Ding Shoutang from the Education Bureau, and Ai Sha and Bian Hanmode, representatives of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, and more than 50 other people attended. At 6:00 PM in the evening, the Municipal Government held another banquet at Chunhua Restaurant. Li Dachao, section chief of the Municipal Government, represented the mayor and delivered a welcome speech. It was not until around 8:00 PM that the banquet ended.

Reception by Various Circles

More than twenty organizations in the city, including the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, the Social Affairs Bureau, the Education Bureau, the Social Education Society, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Farmers' Association, the Shanghai Branch of the Cultural Construction Association, the Shanghai Branch of the Educational Film Association, the Municipal Education Association, the Aviation Association, the China Flying Society, the Air Defense Association, the Northwest Problems Research Association, the Tongjiao Society, the Recreation Association, the Confucius Worship Society, the Chinese and Western Drugstores, the Chenbao Newspaper, the Shanghai News Agency, the Jiangyin Society, Tongminzhi, the Commercial World Bookstore, Shanghai Middle School, and the Alumni Association of the Local Autonomy Training Institute, hosted a tea party at Snow Garden yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. Representatives from various organizations, including Tong Xingbai, Li Dachao, Chen Jicheng, Lu Hailan, Huang Zaoxiong, Yuan Zengyu, Ding Shoutang, Huang Jingzhai, Yang Zhishi, Jing Kui, Zhang Lichun, Yu Zhenhui, Sun Yucai, Zhu Bo, Zhou Bangjun, Zhang Bing, Chen Chengyuan, Zhang Liang, Shi Yi, Ha Decheng, Chen Baidong, Zhu Zhiming, and Zhao Chaoran, and more than 50 other people attended. Ai Sha and Bian Hanmode, representatives of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, also attended the meeting.

Chairman's Speech

First, Chairman Shi Xingbai gave a speech, stating in brief that because Xinjiang is located on the border and transportation is difficult, the situation there is isolated from the interior. Now, seeing Xinjiang compatriots come here, the people of Shanghai are very excited. In the future, we must integrate Xinjiang with the interior. On the one hand, we must develop transportation, and on the other hand, we must communicate culture so that students from Xinjiang can come to the interior to study continuously. They should be able to recognize and train in the language, writing, customs, and habits of the interior to seek national unity and share the responsibility of saving the country. He hopes that everyone will uphold this purpose and work hard in their studies. Then, Wang Yi, a representative of the Hui people, gave a speech, which was translated and relayed by Ai Sha.

Ai Sha's Speech

Next, two Xinjiang representatives gave speeches expressing their gratitude. Then, Ai Sha, a representative of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, gave a speech, stating in brief that because Xinjiang is located in a remote area, they know nothing about the situation in the interior. However, many intellectuals in Xinjiang have new awareness. Without communicating culture with the interior, there is no way to seek the unity of the Chinese nation. Although the Communist Party and others are trying to sabotage in Xinjiang, the people of Xinjiang are not confused by them. In the future, he hopes that the central government can develop the Northwest, so that the future of the people of Xinjiang will be bright. Finally, Li Dachao of the Municipal Government gave a speech, and then they took a photo and dispersed.

Departing for Beijing Last Night

The group of twenty-one Xinjiang students, led by Ai Sha and Bian Hanmode, left Shanghai by overnight express train at 11:00 PM last night. Representatives from various organizations went to the station to see them off. After the students arrive in Beijing, they will be assigned to the Xinjiang Class of Central University, the Central Military Academy, and the Haozang School, respectively.

The Second Issue of Volume Two of Cultural Construction Monthly is Published 132

On the eve of the Sixth Plenary Session, China's political system was being hotly debated. The recently published Cultural Construction Monthly publishes several articles on policy issues. The journal hopes that these articles can guide the Chinese people to grasp the important opportunities of the moment. The first article is Sa Mengwu's "What Kind of Constitution Does China Need?" After dissecting and analyzing the political systems of various countries in the world, it puts forward the central theory that "Chinese people should sacrifice democracy for China, not sacrifice China for democracy." Other articles, such as Cheng Ruilin's "Can China Really Implement Constitutionalism?" and Wang Xinlun's "Strengthening Party Rule and Continuing Political Tutelage," are all based on the current actual situation, hoping to cultivate a correct political concept. In addition, there are two articles on land issues, one is Qi Qisheng's "The Origin of China's Land Problem and Its Countermeasures," and the other is Li Youxi's "Rural Economy and Land Policy in the Song Dynasty," both of which have unique insights and are different from ordinary views. Zhang Sumin's "China's Economy After the Armistice in Italy" analyzes the various phenomena in China's economic circles in recent months in great detail.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (90) 133

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"How do you maintain your life?" This is a very long journey. Aren't you already a grown-up boy?"

"Oh! Before my foot was injured, I was able to get by at first. People gave me food to eat, and I slept in farmhouses. I was always walking on the road during the day. I got lost because I wanted to take a shortcut, otherwise I would have arrived here earlier."

"But if you don't want to come in and live here again, what are you going to do?"

"I originally planned to come and see Tandy and you again: then go back to the city to do my old job, but I am too tired, so I just lay down on the haystack. If you hadn't found me, I would have left here before tomorrow morning."

"Aren't you happy that I found you?" Mrs. Shu looked at him while saying this, with a half-smiling and half-reproachful expression, while kneeling in front of him to examine his injured foot. Color gradually rose on Don's face, but his eyes were always above the bowls and dishes, and at the same time he said very softly: "No, teacher, I am happy, I want to stay, but I am afraid you..."

He didn't finish this sentence because Mama Pei had just arrived in the corridor and saw that his foot was very badly injured, and couldn't help but shout out.

"When did you get hurt?"

"Three days ago."

"Have you been walking in this state?"

"I have a cane. Every time I go to a stream, I wash it. A woman gave me a piece of cloth to temporarily wrap it up."

"Mr. Pei has to come and take a look immediately, and wrap it up properly," Mrs. Shu said, immediately rushing to the next room, deliberately leaving the door half open so that Don could hear everything that was going on.

"Fritz, that child has returned."

"Who? Don?"

"Exactly, Tandy first saw him outside the window, we called him, but he walked away and hid behind the haystack on the lawn. I just found him there, sleeping soundly, because of fatigue and pain, he no longer looks like a person. He ran away from Mr. Bei's side a month ago, and has been walking here ever since. He pretended not to want us to see him, just to come and take a look at us and then go to the city to do his old job. However, it is clear that he hoped to return here, so he did not fear any hardship and came straight here. He is waiting there now, not knowing if you are willing to forgive him and let him return?"

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Success Comes Through Doing 140

— Jian Fen

"No matter what it is: if you don't do it, even if it's easy, you won't succeed; conversely, even if it's difficult, as long as we keep doing it, we will eventually achieve victory." Children: This theory was proposed by Columbus, the discoverer of the New World. Why did he propose this theory? Because after Columbus discovered the New World, when he returned to his hometown, many friends gave him a banquet, partly to celebrate his success and partly to welcome him back. When the banquet was almost over, a friend stood up and said, "Who wouldn't discover a new continent? In my opinion, it's a very easy thing." Columbus heard this and asked a servant to bring an egg and said to that friend, "Friend, now please stand this egg upright!" That friend answered without thinking, "An egg is round and meant to roll. How can it stand upright?" After that friend finished speaking, Columbus calmly pierced a hole in one end of the egg and stood it upright on the table very steadily. When that friend saw Columbus's trick, he arrogantly said, "This is even easier, nothing strange about it; even a child can do it!" Thus, Columbus published the above theory.

Therefore, children, if we want to succeed in something, just talking about it is useless. Only by "doing" can we achieve victory!

Rousseau's Childhood 141

— Yan Chonglou

Rousseau was a great thinker of the eighteenth century and the founder of the study of children's issues. He was the first to advocate the theory of human freedom and equality, making great contributions to society. In particular, concerning children's education, he elaborated on many brilliant treatises. He said: "We should develop children's rights and abilities from childhood." He also said: "We should use the power of example to make children's memories strong and their emotions stable." He also said: "The only means of treating children is natural punishment. For example, if a child breaks a windowpane, the cold wind blowing in will naturally cause the child pain. If this is the case, then the child will know that bad deeds have bad consequences and will definitely strive to improve." Rousseau believed that the power of education could expand children's existence and enable them to continue their activities.

Rousseau was French but was born in Geneva, Switzerland. His father was a watchmaker, and his mother was the daughter of a pastor. Rousseau's mother died after he was born! So he was entirely raised by his father and studied by his father's side. At the age of seven, he liked to read novels. Later, he gradually learned history and biography. He liked to read the biographies of forty-six famous Greeks and Romans. When he was nine years old, his father unfortunately fled because of a lawsuit. So Rousseau lived with relatives. At sixteen, he learned sculpture, but he was not interested, and his master was very abusive. Rousseau could not bear the suffering! So he escaped privately, wandering around France, until his money ran out, and he was in dire straits! Finally, he met someone who helped him and assisted him in making progress. On the one hand, he relied on his tireless efforts, and as a result, he became famous all over the world. Historically, most of the great figures went through hardships and difficulties in their childhood.

Square Eggs 142

— Chen Shicong

I think children must be very strange: where in the world would there be square eggs? Yes, eggs are always oval and never square. However, children, if you do as shown below, you can turn an oval egg into a square one. Today is Sunday, why don't children make this rare thing together!

Changing the shape of an egg is very simple. Just take an egg, put it in rice vinegar, and soak it for a day or two. The eggshell will soften and shrink. Then take a wooden box that matches the size of the egg, put the egg in the box, and soak it in water. In an hour or two, the eggshell will harden. Take it out of the box, and it will become a square egg. If you want to turn it into a triangle or hexagon, you can use the same method. But you just need to prepare models of various shapes in advance.

Children, there is nothing strange about this. It's just using chemistry. Because vinegar contains acid, and this acid has two functions: astringency and erosion, so it makes the eggshell soft and shrinks, changing its shape.

Rural Friends' Daily Life Notes 144

— Ziming

November 5th, Monday, sunny.

The school has changed again. All the class teachers have decorated the classrooms very exquisitely. Each has its own unique interest. Some belong to the magnificent, some express serenity, and some are very beautiful; our children's minds are all attracted by such an environment.

Our seats in the classroom have a certain rule, that is, the baojia (neighborhood self-policing system) grouping; one seat is one household, one row is one jia, with one jiazhang (head of the jia) elected by each household. The jiazhangs in each classroom then elect one baozhang (head of the bao), and the baozhangs of the whole school publicly elect one xiangzhang (head of the xiang). He is the highest leader of our children.

Children in each classroom should abide by various rules, which are all recorded in the baojia regulations. The baojia regulations are signed and sealed by each jiazhang (or with fingerprints), and the head of the household must also join. There is also a joint guarantee, guaranteeing that no accidents or violations of school rules will occur within the bao. If they occur, if one head of household violates school rules, the other heads of household will report to the xiangzhang at any time and submit it to the school. If they conceal and do not report, the heads of household in the same jia will also be subject to the same punishment. Therefore, after the baojia system is implemented, the students are all active on the right track. Moreover, they also understand the meaning of the baojia practiced in society; so I often persuade my neighbors of this principle.

Since our school implemented the baojia, the children no longer have a system of people who specialize in playing. Because we want to handle household registration changes. Therefore, the baojia is a good people's organization in society and a good students' organization in school. Children will all be social people in the future, and this is worthy of our deep attention!

Autumn Leaves 145

— Dazhai

The green leaves are so cute! Once autumn deepens, they will gradually fall, and even the evergreen trees such as pine and cypress contain some autumn meaning, with some old colors, unlike the verdant and green in spring and summer.

Many poets write poems about autumn, describing scenery and emotions, each with its own advantages, but no one has written the reason why the leaves fall in autumn in their poems, which cannot but be considered special; we now study, not only to be elegant literary men, but to be practical scientists; we must not only know the reasons for things on the surface, but we must know the reasons why by research; if things are like the autumn leaves, perhaps there will be some new discoveries in the future; the so-called autumn leaves are just an example.

Speaking of which, why do autumn leaves fall? Because the autumn leaves form a wheel line at the point where they connect to the branch, and this wheel line has a separation tissue, which is composed of several layers of soft cells. After the cells die, the cell membrane is destroyed, and the vascular bundles in the leaf will be cut off by it, so the leaves of the whole tree will gradually fall.

Also, the power of the sun in autumn is weak, and the heat of the sun cannot make the tree absorb enough nutrients. In addition, the weather in autumn is relatively dry, so it needs to evaporate more water. Since it is difficult for the tree to absorb nutrients, it has to save consumption, so it cuts off part of the leaves—the nutrient-consuming organs—to save nutrients and keep them for winter use. When spring comes, it will slowly return to its original state, and it will be green branches again.

Children's Science Lecture Book—(2) Printing and Binding 146

— Lin Yin

Last time I talked about the printing of a book, which is an important record of cultural history. However, there is still a drawback to printing like that. That is, after a book is printed, the typesetter must return the type to the original type case (Figure 1). The next time it is reprinted, it must be typeset in the same way, and typesetting and printing take a long time. In addition, after the type is heavily pressed by the printing press, it gradually wears out, and the strokes are not clear the next time it is used. So an Englishman, Stanhope, invented the clay plate in 1804. He covered the type bed with clay, pressed it into a negative, and then poured molten lead into a positive lead plate (Figure 2) for printing, which was much more convenient. However, keeping the lead plate is very expensive, and the clay plate is easily broken after melting and pouring. That year, the Frenchman Xero invented the paper plate, so only the paper mold needs to be preserved, and there is no need to keep the lead plate. The printing industry has moved further on the road to progress.

That method of typesetting and printing is called movable type printing. It was originally invented in China. However, the Chinese themselves did not know how to improve it. When it was transmitted to Europe, after foreign research, it was re-transmitted to China, and we had to learn their methods instead.

Put the lead plate on the printing frame, brush it with ink, and cover it with white paper, and you can print it out sheet by sheet. After printing, it must be taken for binding. The first step in binding is to arrange the page numbers. Arrange the printed sheets in order according to the page numbers. The name for this in binding is called arranging the book (Figure 3). After arranging, bind them with thread or use a machine to bind them with lead wire (Figure 4). Then put on the cover, and it becomes a book. But it must go through a cutting process to make the four sides of the book neat (Figure 5). In this way, a book is completed.

Stone Mortar Great Immortal 147

— Teacher Artisan

In a remote rural village, there lived ten or so farming families. During the busy farming season in summer, the farmers all went to work in the fields. One of them had an old stone mortar in their field. Near noon, a dark cloud suddenly appeared in the sky, and soon there was lightning, thunder, and a heavy rain. Coincidentally, a passerby passed by there, opened a paper umbrella, and temporarily sat in the stone mortar to wait for the rain to pass before continuing on. After a while, the rain became heavier, and a large amount of water accumulated. When the rain stopped and the sky cleared, the head of the household returned home and suddenly discovered that the stone mortar was completely dry, without a single drop of rainwater. Such a heavy rain fell, so why was there not a drop of water in the stone mortar? Wasn't this because an immortal had descended to protect the stone mortar? Everyone in the village came to watch, and everyone said that the stone mortar was very old and must have become an immortal.

A poor Taoist nearby deliberately pretended to be mysterious and fabricated stories, publicizing it, and erected a flagpole with a pennant, calling it the "Stone Mortar Great Immortal." Soon people from all directions came to offer incense and worship. The Taoist collected incense money, and in less than two years, he actually built a temple to enshrine the stone mortar. It became famous far and wide, and was effective in one region.

The passerby passed through the old place again for the second time and suddenly saw the newly built Stone Mortar Great Immortal Temple, with many pious men and women offering incense and worshiping inside. Inquiring about the reason, he couldn't help but smile. He told everyone the story of sitting in the stone mortar to avoid the rain two years ago. Everyone suddenly understood. From then on, the Stone Mortar Great Immortal was no longer effective.

Magic Cage 148

— Wen Yuyang

The magic cage is a moving toy. It can change and can also be considered a simple magic trick. Children, when you make it to play, cut the picture in the newspaper as it is and stick it on the original cardboard. Fill in the colors according to the numbers, or you can draw it on the cardboard and do the same way, and it will become a very interesting toy.

First, you need to prepare all kinds of materials, scissors, chisels, thick cardboard, colored glue. After you prepare the materials, cut out the picture (1) and picture (2) in the newspaper and stick them on the original cardboard. Still, cut the cardboard as it is. After the glue is slightly dry, use a chisel to dig out the blank of picture (1) according to the lines, in the order of the numbers (red, yellow, blue, green). Then insert the left and right ends of picture (2) into the left and right narrow holes of picture (1), as shown in picture (3). Move your hands left and right, and it will be very fun!

The Story of the White Mountain Crow (9) 150

— Xi

Just as I was about to fly away, the turtledove suddenly opened its eyes again. It said to me: "Goodbye! You are tired of singing. My name is Groli. I hope you remember me often!"

I hurriedly replied: "Beautiful Groli, you are gentle and lovely. I am willing to live for you and even die for you, but your feathers are peach-colored, and I don't have such good fortune!"

(4)

I flew back to Paris with a belly full of questions. As I was flying, my head suddenly bumped into the head of another bird, who was flying over from the other side. This bump was unexpected and very fierce, causing both of us to crash onto a treetop. Fortunately, we didn't fall to the ground. I steadied myself and looked at the other side, thinking that he would definitely quarrel with me. When I saw him, I saw that he was a crow of all colors, his neck seemed to be bigger than mine, and he had a high crown on his forehead, showing a heroic spirit. His face was raised high in the air, with a proud and arrogant look, but he didn't mean to quarrel with me. We greeted each other politely, apologized to each other, and started talking. I first asked him his name and also asked him which country he flew from.

He said to me: "I'm surprised, you didn't recognize me, maybe you and we are not of the same kind?"

I replied: "Sir, to tell you the truth, I don't know which kind I belong to. Everyone always asks me like this. They must be betting on me there."

"You're kidding," he said, "I saw your feathers and knew you were my brothers. You certainly belong to that very famous and very respected white parrot family." (To be continued)

I am Not Discouraged 151

— Zhang Dejun, Sixth Grader of Shanghai Xinye Primary School

The Children's Year Implementation Committee organized a children's speech contest, and the main topic of the speech was: "About Children's Year and Relief to Children in Disaster Areas." I felt quite interested in speaking, so I eagerly asked my teacher to sign me up to prepare for the topic. After two weeks of practice and guidance from the teacher and criticism from the students, I excitedly attended the speech contest held at the People's Education Center on the 28th of last month with my classmate Shen Yaqin. That day, according to the chairman's report, "more than eighty people attended." I thought: There are so many talented people, I definitely have no hope of winning. But, thinking about it, my speech was not bad; the teachers and friends also criticized me that my speaking and posture were not bad either, I thought maybe there was a glimmer of hope! After all the children had finished speaking, after a while, the chairman announced the rankings, calling out the numbers one by one. When they called them all, my number was not there, and my heart jumped. I failed. At that time, I was very ashamed, resentful, and almost cried. The teachers and friends tried their best to comfort me, what is there to be ashamed of, failure is the mother of success, as long as you work hard in the future, if you have the opportunity, you will definitely have a good harvest. I thought: That's right, why be discouraged? So I am still very interested in speaking now and I am not discouraged.

However, this ruling, which concerns experiments to remove the New Deal, was enough to ignite the enthusiasm of the current anti-New Deal sentiment. Therefore, the market trend ultimately rose again. Small exchange stock indices also rose, and the bond market was active, with public utility bonds being particularly strong. The total daily transaction volume was 3.35 million shares. River Storage Increases, Rice Prices Fall Again by About Half a Yuan 162

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, there were more than fifty suppliers (with a total of over ten thousand piculs), with Bo Dao rice being the most abundant, followed by new Japonica. However, the new grains were damp and soft and could not be stored for long, leading to a continuous surge in supply. With thick accumulations in the wharves, sellers were eager to sell, resulting in an extremely sluggish market and a further price decline. Early Japonica rice varieties such as Hou Zao continued to drop by five or six cents, and new Bo Dao rice fell by six or seven cents. Only the Bao Xiao Jin Qing gang took the opportunity to purchase, reaching over two thousand bags, so the high-quality grains were two or three cents higher than the lower-quality ones. Du Jian rice followed the drop by six cents, and foreign Jian rice fell by seven or eight cents. Although this price decrease occurred during the period of falling orders, it also presented the same pattern. Only Yin Yuan rice, due to its scarcity, recovered slightly by a few cents. Looking at the overall trend, with the abundant accumulation and the pessimistic sentiment, it would be difficult to stabilize.

(North Shanghai) There were fifty-six or fifty-seven suppliers, with more than twenty or thirty boats stored in the river. Various grains in the market were unpopular, and the morning market was exceptionally quiet. Later, due to customers bidding low and demanding sales, the market price of new Japonica high-quality grains dropped by two or three cents, and medium-quality grains fell by three or four cents. Bai Ge Bo Dao rice was sold off at varying prices, from five to seven cents. Foreign Jian high-quality grains dropped by a small two or three cents, and medium-quality grains also dropped by a small amount. Du Jian and Bu Jian rice followed the drop by a small two or three cents. Bai Yuan rice continued to arrive, but retail sales were not active, also dropping by a small three or four cents. Bran and other grains also decreased by about two cents.

Customer Xian Rice Continues to Fall, Foreign Rice Stagnates 163

Yesterday, both foreign rice and customer Xian rice markets became quiet. Foreign rice was held up by merchants, and buyers were cautious, resulting in no single bag transactions. Customer Xian rice continued to arrive, but merchants had already stopped purchasing. The Northern Ocean Gang's stored rice had not yet been fully loaded, and new transactions were also halted. Due to the increasing number of boats arriving from the river, prices had already fallen. Also, with the recent rumors subsiding, consumers no longer resumed stockpiling. As a result, the market had limited demand. Only 130 bags of Yong rice, 400 bags of Wen Tai rice, and 100 bags of Ji rice were sold in the entire market. Yong late rice fell slightly due to its high price, while Wen Tai rice fell slightly by three or four cents due to the large amount of stock and arrivals. Other rice types were sluggish by one or two cents. All were handled by the market.
