Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Musings

On Unity 170

— Zou Hui

In his closing remarks at the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, Committee Member Yu Youren said, "...Successive floods and droughts, the tense international environment, and the impact of global economic changes are increasing the difficulties faced by our nation, already severely troubled. We cannot deny the hardship of the struggles and efforts made by the entire nation over the past ten months, but we must point out that to overcome this extremely difficult period, we still need greater sincerity and unity, and we need ten or a hundred times more effort. To save the nation and ensure its survival, we must concentrate national power and enrich the people's strength, using our own struggling power to overcome the difficulties of the environment..." These words are truly what everyone wants to say and are the hopes that everyone cherishes day and night. The so-called "sincerity," the so-called "unity," and the so-called "power of self-struggle" are undoubtedly the only driving forces for China's renewal amidst the current national crisis.

"But what exactly constitutes true unity? Although this has become a cliché, in today's high tide of calls for unity, it is indeed necessary to re-evaluate its value. In the past, the banner of unity has been hoisted by those in power, and the conch shell of unity has been blown by those with influence, but in the end, the conch shell was broken, the banner was shattered, and the situation of disintegration reappeared. Therefore, a union based on temporary interests cannot escape being a mere alliance of convenience and is definitely not unity. Today, the trend of promoting national unity for the great goal of jointly overcoming the national crisis is certainly gratifying, but we still cannot help but hope that a true 'affectionate sincerity' can arise between every member, like a natural adhesive creating a cohesive and solidifying effect. Only in this way can we be united forever and never separated.

To achieve true unity, we believe that at least the following three points should be met:

1. Group consciousness: We humans live under the social organization of a group of people, and individuals cannot go beyond the influence of society. Therefore, individualism and free action often hinder the common order of the masses, and the eruption of individual desires is the main culprit in undermining the group. Therefore, to realize the great premise of unity, we must absolutely abandon egoism and cultivate a concept of always being for the group.

2. Spirit of sacrifice: The so-called sacrifice contains two major meanings: first, from a negative perspective, in order to complete the will or welfare of the group, one must first sacrifice one's own opinions or interests; second, from a positive perspective, for the happiness and benefit of the public, as a member of the group, we must not stand idly by and watch success or failure, but should go through fire and water without hesitation. This is the expression of a positive spirit of sacrifice.

3. Disciplined life: A romantic lifestyle manifested in the spirit is bound to be scattered and disorderly. Disorder and lack of discipline are fatal to unity. Only by cultivating a strict and disciplined life can we stimulate scattered hearts and unite separated wills.

Humanity's need for unity did not begin today. From ancient times to the present, those who unite survive, and those who are individual perish.

Page 20

This has almost become an iron principle of history. In the ancient, uncivilized era, wild beasts roamed the land, and an individual's strength could not match the fierce beasts. Thus, the phenomenon of living in groups arose, which is the original symbol of unity. Later, the concept of family arose, uniting clans to resist other clans. Then, nationalism arose, uniting one nation to compete with other nations. A history of humanity seems to be nothing but a record of unity. Originally, the destiny of humanity lies not in mutual struggle, but in mutual compassion; not in mutual exclusion, but in mutual assistance. People should offer a naked heart to each other, proceeding towards our common goal. However, even today, there are still a few ambitious individuals on earth with stubborn minds, who are still dreaming of inflicting cruelty on others. For the sake of the great unity of all humanity, we must take bold actions to eliminate the rebellious elements. On the one hand, we should unite the strength of our people to seek self-reliance. On the other hand, we must unite the oppressed nations of the world to fight together. As the Western saying goes, "Unity is strength." Looking at Abyssinia today, I am even more convinced.

Hobbies 171

— Li

I often encounter friends who are not yet well-acquainted wanting me to join their mahjong battles at a certain time, but these good intentions are all rejected by my strange habit of never playing mahjong. The reason I don't know how to play mahjong is because I didn't have a suitable learning environment growing up, but that's not entirely true. My grandfather and uncles were all very enthusiastic about playing mahjong, and in my childhood, my grandfather often took me to sit quietly by one corner of their table, watching them shuffle and sort the tiles. They played with great enthusiasm, from noon to dusk, from night to late at night, and I could even sit with them until midnight. I understood the terms for the different tile suits early on, like "Wan," "Suo," and "Tong." I also understood what "Pong," "Chi," and "Hu" meant, as well as how to do them, but I never played mahjong.

Some people would laugh at me for this, saying, how can you be a modern person if you don't even know how to play mahjong? Mahjong skills are an essential skill in social situations. In their eyes, someone who doesn't know how to play mahjong is simply a modern cripple, not qualified to be a modern person! Besides, some people say: Most writers are enthusiastic gamblers. Cao Juren even discovered a theory of contingent history at the Jai-alai stadium and established his own school of thought! Isn't it a literary joke if someone who writes doesn't know how to play mahjong? Indeed, I'm not keen on being a so-called modern person, nor do I want to be a writer, so mahjong doesn't have to be associated with me.

But I do have an interest in drinking alcohol, that's definitely true.

Five years ago, it could be said that I was at the peak of my drinking days. At that time, the worries of life were strangling my heart, and my fragile heartstrings were so easily moved. At that time, I only felt the need to cry out loud, to roar, but those threads of worry only tightened, tightened even more! At that time, the only way to temporarily forget my sorrows was to drink bowl after bowl of yellow wine. Every night, a packet of peanuts, five or six pieces of dried tofu, and five or six catties of strong, rich Shaoxing wine were divided and poured into the stomachs of two or three of my colleagues! After each catty, everyone's faces were flushed, but mine became even paler. After wild singing and shouting, everyone's shouts for more wine became even more frequent. From then on, my fragile soul became even more fragile, easily moved and easily angered, like the emotions of a woman suffering from hysteria! One night, I was still drinking with two or three colleagues to drown my sorrows, but who knew that as the wine fell into my stomach, tears poured from my eyes. I cried and screamed wildly all night, and my colleagues were helpless.

At that time, I was a famous drunk with a capacity for two catties of alcohol. Whenever there was an opportunity to drink, people would always treat me as someone who could handle two catties of alcohol, so they would keep pouring until I was heavily intoxicated. I myself seemed to always generously perform the idiotic state of a drunken madman. But every time I drank, my painful heart only became more painful. My drinking was not like the elegant act of immortal Li Bai.

Times change, and my old drinking companions have scattered. I myself wander around Shanghai, and the hardships I experience are no less than those of that time. However, the years have taught me year after year, leading me to change from "naive extravagance" to "silent sorrow." Although I sometimes miss the delicious taste of fine wine, I rarely have the extravagant feelings of those years anymore.

In this silent sorrow, I am being urged to grow old day by day.

Travel Weekly

Hot Springs Park 172

— Bo

In Sichuan, whether it's in rural villages or cities, there's really nothing to speak of in terms of construction plans. Cultural backwardness means they lack new scientific knowledge, and economic decline means they lack the resources to engage in construction. But everyone who has been to Sichuan will remember one place name – Beibei. This is a new place, the only one in Sichuan built with new methods and scientific planning, specifically for recreation.

Lu Zuofu, formerly the general manager of Minsheng Industrial Company and recently appointed Director of the Sichuan Construction Department, is the founder of Beibei. He spent several years painstakingly decorating it with his personal funds. In a short time, it has become so beautiful.

Beibei – now the collective name for Beibei Town and Hot Springs Park – is located on the south bank of the Jialing River, less than a hundred li from Chongqing. Originally, Beibei was fifteen li away from the hot springs, but since the hot springs were renovated, their names have become intertwined. Now, when people say Beibei, they undoubtedly mean Hot Springs Park.

This time, I was fortunate enough to go to Chongqing and stay for a week. Chongqing is such a dirty and noisy place that if the ropes of life didn't bind people to this city, they certainly wouldn't stay long. So, after staying in Chongqing for three days, one morning I quietly took a steamer with a suitcase and set off for Beibei.

The steamer belongs to Minsheng Company, which also monopolizes the Jialing River route. Every morning at five o'clock, two steamers leave along the Jialing River for Hechuan, returning from Hechuan the next day. Beibei is located between Chongqing and Hechuan.

The boat left very early, before six o'clock. The boat was so crowded and noisy, and the heavy sound of the engine made my head heavy. There were no berths on the boat because the journey was too short, less than a day. So I leaned on the railing, quietly watching the green hills and waves slowly moving behind me.

A middle-aged man experienced in traveling stood beside me unexpectedly. We didn’t depart from the usual polite convention of meeting on a journey, and soon started talking. According to what he told me, the boat we were taking was going upstream; it takes eight or nine hours from Chongqing to Hechuan, but coming back, it only takes five or six hours. "Aren't you going to the hot springs?" he said to me. "I am too. We won't arrive until twelve noon! But when we come back, we'll take the boat leaving from Hechuan at seven in the morning, and we'll arrive in Chongqing after ten."

The water flowed very fast, and sometimes the boat shook violently, like an old man with a fever. There was one place where the boat moved very strangely, making a large "之" (zhi) character on the river, not sailing in the middle of the river. I asked someone, and he said: This is because there are stones under the water, so it has to go around in bends, looking like a dog's crippled leg, so this place is called Dog Leg Bend. The boat cannot sail on Dog Leg Bend; it has to go around it in a "之" character. Every year, many wooden boats are destroyed here, and countless lives are lost.

He pointed out a place to me on the north bank of the river, in a very high mountain recess, where the only railway in all of Sichuan is located. This railway is specifically for transporting coal, and the Minsheng Company's coal plant is located there. I looked up and saw several smoking chimneys on the high mountainside. At this moment, a train was passing on the mountainside, and then disappeared behind another mountain. It looked very small, like a small black snake. My middle-aged companion told me that the Minsheng Company has thirty-some ships, large and small, all using coal produced by its own plant.

The boat arrived at Beibei Town and stopped for a few minutes. Looking from the river, Hot Springs Park was already visible.

Fifteen minutes later, I arrived at Hot Springs Park.

This is a mountain. Looking up, all the houses, sports fields, and orchards are clearly visible. After disembarking, I prepared to face the wide stone steps made of mountain bluestone. There are trees on both sides of the stone steps, especially bamboo. After climbing about two hundred steps, you begin to see the terraces carved out of the mountains by people. I chose a room in a very delicate small Western-style house and began to rest. The room faced the big river, with high mountains on the opposite side and behind. It was named Count Sail Building. This is good; at dusk, counting the sailing boats coming and going on the river is quite poetic.

Afterwards, I began my tour. This Hot Springs Park covers a width of about two li, and its position is exactly halfway up the mountain. There are now many Western-style houses specifically for the convenience of travelers, such as Moon-Viewing Building, Flower-Appreciating Building, and Sunrise Pavilion, which stands tall on the mountaintop but few people climb to. There are many meadows, always with artificial streams and various fruit trees. The hot spring water in the streams is hot. To the east, there is a waterfall cascading down, wrapping around a kudzu vine, with a very beautiful shape. Naturally, the water from this waterfall is also hot.

Later, I hurriedly walked along the cement path towards the public hot spring bath. The bathhouse is divided into rooms and a swimming pool, and the swimming pool is divided into an inner and outer pool. The inner pool only has water up to a person's armpits, but the outer pool can be used to practice diving. As for the private bath rooms, they are specifically for shy ladies and older people; young men rarely want to spend an extra dime to try them (the swimming pool only costs a dime). All the water is brought down from the mountainside through bamboo pipes; the water in both the private bath rooms and the swimming pool is flowing. It flows in freely and flows out freely to a certain limit. And the water temperature is determined by God to be only one degree higher than the average human body temperature.

I paid a dime, and the attendant gave me a pair of blue cloth shorts specially prepared for guests. I changed in the changing room, put on these cloth shorts, and walked down to the inner pool. This pool is very suitable for people like me who can't swim; it won't drown you, and the house covers it so the sun won't tan your white skin. The pool is about twenty yards long and about the same width. The water flows down from a hole in the eastern corner, like a small waterfall. Many people stand under it, letting the rushing water splash countless water droplets on their backs. "This is really a good idea," I thought after looking around. The spring water flows naturally into the inner pool, and when the inner pool is full, it naturally flows into the outer pool, and when the outer pool reaches a certain limit, it flows down the mountain into the Jialing River. This requires no one to look after it.

After the bath, beautiful dusk arrived. At my feet, above my head, in front of me, behind me, and to my left and right, were the sounds of birds returning to the forest. The mountains across the river gradually turned dark green, and a new moon climbed out from the mountain peak behind us.

How can you blame Beibei for being called the "Little Three Gorges"? Look, the mountains on both banks are so high and so steep, and the water is so turbulent; when you walk here, wouldn't you think that the Goddess Peak is right next to you?

Lectures on Social Science

Labor Tools 173

— Jingxing

So-called labor tools are tools used to transmit human labor to act upon natural matter, to overcome natural matter, and to change its shape, function, and so on. In ancient times, there were stone tools, knives, axes, saws, hammers, and in modern times, there are complex and massive machines that have been improved and developed. Although labor tools are already completed, artificially transformed, dead matter, these things contain extremely large effects and social significance for humans and a given society. Although some modern sociologists use the Stone Age, Bronze Age, and Iron Age to divide social eras, it is inevitably narrow and not entirely appropriate, but from this, we can see the importance of the position of labor tools in the process of human social life.

Generally speaking, labor tools are not only a bridge for the exchange between humans and natural matter but also a manifestation of the civilization or barbarity of people and their social life. When considering a single, individual labor tool as the object of investigation, it is certainly still a completed, artificially transformed, dead material mass, a solidified product of labor, but if many individual labor tools are linked together for a historical examination, then this thing itself exhibits a kind of vitality, a kind of evolutionary life's inherent continuous movement, even embodying the evolutionary movement of humans and their society.

The human body is a living organic entity; as for labor tools, no matter how much they contain human labor within them, in the end, they are still just dead inorganic matter (excluding cattle, horses, and livestock, of course), two completely different kinds of things. However, the fact is very interesting: the latter, inorganic material labor tools, can replace the physiological evolution of the former, organic human beings. Because labor tools are, in fact, simply extensions and transformations of human organs, the improvement and evolution of labor tools can replace the improvement and progress of human organs. For example, according to human needs, we must be able to see the vast sky and observe microorganisms smaller than the tip of an autumn hair, so human eyes need to be greatly improved. At least they should be like cat's eyes, with extremely large contractile variability in their pupils. However, humans, because of the invention of telescopes and microscopes, have these labor tools to replace the improving function of the naked eye, so even if our eyes do not undergo such major changes, we can see extremely distant celestial bodies and observe material particles and microorganisms invisible to the naked eye. Pincers are the transformation of fingers; they replace the function of pulling nails by hand. Saw teeth are the transformation of teeth; they also replace the function of cutting things with teeth. Rakes are the transformation of fingernails; they also replace the function of grabbing things with fingernails. So, with pliers, saws, and rakes, there is no longer a need for developed fingers, sharp teeth, or sharp claws. This is proof that labor tools have replaced the improvement and progress of physiological organs. Thus, all labor tools are merely extensions, transformations, and diversification and complexity of human organs outside the body.

Labor tools replacing the evolution of human physiological organs is only one aspect of their function. On the other hand, they can also change human physiological organization; people create labor tools, and labor tools can then come back and transform people. Because the human body organization, in the continuous change of labor tools, must adapt to this change to change itself. For example, if someone asks why humans don't grow tiger or leopard-like sharp claws, then we say that humans, because of the invention of pliers and rakes, not only don't need such claws, but according to Lamarck's theory of use and disuse, they will naturally degenerate because pliers and rakes have replaced their function, and furthermore, having them would restrict the function of gripping things and doing other things. Also, if someone asks why human brains are particularly developed, then we say it is because humans have various labor tools, making our labor work, methods, processes, and even labor objects complex and vast, so the brain, in this complex labor life, cannot adapt to this life without gradually changing everything about itself. From this, it can be seen that labor tools are also constantly transforming human natural organs and bodies. The evolution of labor tools, on the natural part of human beings, represents him as being savage or civilized, also pushes human nature from savagery to the realm of civilization, away from the animal stage.

The fact that labor tools represent the evolution of human beings themselves is certainly obvious, but it is not as obvious as the fact that labor tools represent the evolution of social culture. Because human labor itself, no matter how great its use value, how great its ability to control nature, must be mediated by labor tools to reach the point of applying its labor to the external world and conquering and utilizing nature on a large scale according to its needs and purposes, in order to transfer and transmit it in the past, thereby changing natural objects. Therefore, labor tools are the medium for the transfer of the use value of human labor, the tool for transmitting labor. With them, humans can widely use external matter to improve their lives, to build a rich social material, that is, to enrich the social economic life. However, the material economic life of society is certainly the culture of society, and the richness of all spiritual life, the improvement and evolution of all cultural relics and systems, are based on the changes in the most basic economic life. Therefore, the evolutionary stage of the overall culture of society, the civilization or barbarity of society, just like the civilization or savagery, progress or backwardness of human natural bodies themselves, can be expressed by the degree of diversity, complexity, refinement, and crudeness of labor tools. If labor tools are rudimentary and simple, then the economic life of this society will inevitably be very crude and simple, and all social culture will be equally backward. Conversely, then society will have evolved to a high degree of civilization. We only need to observe that the primitive era used stone tools as labor tools, becoming savages and savage social life and culture, and that modern labor tools have developed to extreme complexity and diversity, and modern social culture has also advanced to a very complex height, to understand this.

The improvement, progress, and complexity of labor tools not only can simply transfer labor and its use value but also enable the action of human labor to extend to a wider range of natural objects, to control a wider range of natural objects, and even to enhance human labor efficiency. Therefore, using stone tools not only cannot subdue the power of water and electricity in the universe for human use, but also using stone tools to fell a tree would require a lot of labor and time. This means that using bad labor tools limits the production capacity greatly, and the progress of labor tools represents the development process of social productive forces. The more backward labor tools are, the smaller human production capacity is. The more advanced labor tools are, the stronger human productive forces are. The development of productive forces is determined by the degree of improvement of labor tools. However, the development of productive forces determines all the development processes of society, so the evolution of labor tools can also determine and represent the general development of social culture here.

As for the relationship between people, strictly speaking, the determining role of labor tools also participates in it. Because the formation of human society lies in the need for labor production, and especially the existence of social public labor tools, in order to carry out social production. People's own organs are the personal property of individuals and cannot be made public for social use. Others cannot use my hands and feet to hit people or walk for themselves. Only the extra-corporeal organs that are the social products that are separate from personal ownership can be used in common. Therefore, the social relationship of collective human labor is promoted by the common use of labor tools. Without common, usable labor tools, there can be no common labor, social production cannot be established, and human relationships cannot be linked together. Not only that, if you examine that the use of stone tools cannot produce more products than personal life requires, the exploitation of slavery cannot occur, and how the emergence of modern large-scale mechanical industrial system necessarily requires the free labor buying and selling methods of the wage system, and the various social relations produced thereby, then you can know that the changes in labor tools also cause human relationships to constantly undergo corresponding changes. In short, labor tools not only become a symbol of the civilization and evolution of natural human beings but also become an indicator of the progress of social civilization. They determine the degree of development of social productive forces and also become a determining factor in the generation and change of human relationships themselves.

Special Self-Employment Introduction

Please Don't Worry About Me Limping Around Looking For A Job 174

— Wu Hesheng

I am the most painful person in the world because my life is flawed. Early on, I lost the ability to move part of my leg. At the same time, I have encountered the most difficult hurdle in the world because I am unemployed, and it has been almost half a year.

Although I am disabled, I have done a lot of things: After my father sent me to a Shanghai cigarette paper store to learn the trade, I then entered a woodworking shop and a shoe store as a shop assistant; I served as an accountant and manager in stationery companies and wineries; I worked as a copyist, draftsman, and mimeographer in cultural institutions... Naturally, I have gone through many difficult hurdles in the process. Each time I was unemployed and changed jobs, I was always threatened by life. However, I always took heavy steps, buried my head with a resolute heart, like Wu Zixu passing through the checkpoints, breaking through one after another. I even congratulated myself on breaking out of the circle of small apprentices and gradually climbing to the office of a high-level cultural institution! Who would have thought that I would be unemployed again! It turns out that the higher you climb (?), the harder you fall!

Once unemployed in Shanghai, I have been busy with this matter every day, asking people to help me find something to do in the east and asking people to help me find work in the west. What is the result of asking people? "There are too many unemployed people now, not to mention someone who is limping like you!" "They all say they don't want someone who is limping because it is unsightly!" People use these words to answer me, with a hint of resentment in their tone that I shouldn't have bothered them to suffer such humiliation on my behalf. I naturally have nothing to say; therefore, there has never been a success.

There are many unemployed people, I think that's right. No one can avoid this in today's society. But why say "not to mention someone who is limping like you"? And why say "it is unsightly"? Does my limping mean that I can't do things? Is it because I am "limping" and offend the sight of the adults and gentlemen that I don't have the right to look for a job in this world? God! What kind of world is this? Does that mean I am only worthy of a dead end with no job forever? Does my limping mean that I don't even have the hope of survival?

Resentment is your resentment, I will do it myself, because this world is a snobbish world. If you have money and power, then even if you are limping or paralyzed all over, it doesn't matter. People might even admire you. Basically, it is because I was born with a bad life (if you say there is fate), I have no money, let alone power, and my limping does not receive people's welcome, but instead incurs hatred, which is inevitable.

But, is this world only filled with snobbish worshippers? I don't believe it! I don't believe it! I believe I can live on, I believe that those friends who see the truth through snobbery will sympathize with me! Pity me!

Respected friends! Are you willing to let my life be destroyed in front of you? Give me work! I can still work, and I can still help you complete your work.

P.S.: No matter what kind of work, I am willing to do it well with my enthusiasm and my strength (I can handle jobs such as hawker, apprentice, shop assistant, copyist, steel pen, mimeograph, drawing advertisements, drawing patterns, etc. in cultural institutions). Please don't worry about me limping around. Five li is okay. My body is very healthy, and I can also handle labor work. I have no various hobbies. Finally, naturally, I don't care about the salary, I only ask for room and board.

Mailing address: Amature Weekly Newspaper Office.

Amateur Coffee Corner

On Intellectuals 175

— Heng

Due to the determination of living conditions, intellectuals cannot become an independent group of people: every intellectual is subordinate to or close to a certain independent group of people. Conversely, it can also be said that every independent group of people has its spokespersons in various aspects (such as politics, philosophy (literature))—intellectuals; the so-called intellectuals generally, that is, the scholars we called in the past, refer to the spokespersons or sympathizers of a certain independent group of people. Therefore, it is usually incorrect for people to call intellectuals the intellectual class. In fact, Confucius and Mencius, as well as Yang Zhu and Mo Di, were all scholars, but we cannot say that they were the same group; Zeng Guofan and Liang Qichao, Lin Qinnan and Hu Shi were also intellectuals, but we cannot say that they were one group.

Because every independent group of people has its intellectuals, the social movements led by them will inevitably have intellectuals participating. Intellectuals naturally cannot lead a social movement alone, complete a great historical mission, but without them, no social movement will happen, develop, or be completed. If the "May Fourth" Movement did not have Chen Duxiu and Hu Shi, there would naturally be other intellectuals to replace their duties, but if there were no intellectuals participating at all (this assumption will certainly not become a reality), then the occurrence of the "May Fourth" Movement would probably also be a big problem. "Scholars rebel, it won't be successful in three years," but without "scholars," even if someone wants to rebel, they won't be able to. Song Jiang, known as the Timely Rain, was famous all over the world, but without the "lazy scholar" Wu Yong, his position as the first leader in Liangshan Village would probably be unstable; Liu Bei was handsome, but without Zhuge Liang, whose Daoist name was Crouching Dragon, he probably wouldn't be able to claim himself emperor in Shu; Zhang Liang, Chen Ping, and other intellectuals contributed greatly to the Han Gaozu's gaining of the empire; the success of King Wu's conquest of Zhou, his so-called "ten rebellious ministers" also made great contributions; all of these are sufficient to fully demonstrate the social role of intellectuals. Therefore, although intellectuals are detached and cannot play an independent role, we cannot underestimate them and say that they are useless because of this; the saying "scholars are useless in everything" does not correspond to objective facts.

Intellectuals are detached; they can climb up or fall down. They can enter the conservative camp and work hard to turn back the clock, but they can also become members of a progressive group and promote historical progress. In history, there are naturally many intellectuals who serve as slaves to evil people, betray themselves and harm others, and endanger the country and society, but as history progresses, it is not impossible to find scholars who are not moved by the oppression of authority and the temptation of money and who are always faithful to objective truth. Therefore, we cannot, because we see a few opportunistic "sell-out" scholars in history, affirm that "scholars have no integrity," and say that all intellectuals are the most unreliable, opportunistic, and evil people!

At the same time, every social movement that occurs must have its objective social conditions. As for intellectuals participating in or representing a certain group to lead a progressive social movement, it is because they have recognized the trend of social development and change in their social life, and recognized the significance of the social movement that is happening or about to happen at that time, and it is not because they want to fight for some status for all intellectuals that they do so. In fact, every progressive social movement, although many intellectuals can recognize its significance and participate in it, at the same time, some intellectuals fail to recognize its significance and express their opposition. For example, the Northern Expedition of the National Revolution was participated in by many intellectuals, but also opposed by many intellectuals. If intellectuals are regarded as an independent group, and it is said that their participation in a...

Continued on page 5

Page 22

Page 23

...competing for status, and thus evaluate the participation of intellectuals in social movements with a purely "selfish" attitude, completely negating the role of intellectuals and even their personality, then how should the above-mentioned events be explained? Here, I hope that people who despise intellectuals will use their brains a little more!

Of course, even among the intellectuals who participate in progressive social movements, there are some who climb up by taking advantage of the development of the movement; after they climb up or when they want to climb up, they often use regressive behavior to obtain their personal and realistic interests. However, even so, we cannot deny the significance of the movement, nor can we deny the achievements of the intellectuals who participated in the movement; it is wrong to deny the significance of the movement because some intellectuals who participated in the progressive social movement "sell themselves out" midway or later, or to oppose the movement and the intellectuals who participated in the movement because of this, saying that although the movement is meaningful, the intellectuals who participated in the movement cannot be evaluated in the same way as the significance of the movement. We know that the significance of a progressive social movement exists objectively and will never disappear because a few people participate and then "sell themselves out" later. For example, some of the intellectuals who participated in the Xinhai Revolution later went on to support Yuan Shikai as emperor, but history will not fail to record the objective significance of the Xinhai Revolution because of this. At the same time, before we evaluate an event, we should base it on the objective effects of the event, not on our own subjective guesses. If an intellectual has participated in a certain progressive social movement, then even if he retreats midway or later, history will truthfully record his participation in that social movement, and will evaluate its significance in the same way as the significance of that movement; because the objective effect of his efforts when he participated in that movement is beneficial to the development of the movement, and will never disappear because of his retreat midway or later, just as his participation in that progressive social movement cannot conceal his retreat midway or later. Take Dr. Hu Shi as an example. In the "May Fourth" Literary Revolution, he was progressive, and he made great contributions to the New Culture Movement at that time. Now, he is still obsessed with the cultural relics and systems of the gold and yuan dynasties and has long been outdated, but...cannot...publicly deny his past achievements, nor can...cover up his current...outdatedness because of his past achievements. Therefore, it is unfair and erroneous for people to rely on their own subjective guesses and say that the motives of an intellectual who once participated in a progressive social movement were impure when he participated in the movement, thereby denying the significance of his participation in the movement, and even saying that the movement itself is problematic.

I think that intellectuals are detached, their will is relatively weak, they lack courage and魄力, they can speak and think, but they lack the spirit of practical work, so they themselves have many shortcomings. We should not nitpick and excessively鞭打 them, but should guide them to serve the country and society well. If they have shortcomings and mistakes, we should naturally point them out to make them pay attention, but we cannot deny their active role. Of course, those intellectuals who consciously work hard to turn back the clock, live a decadent and depraved life, and engage in activities that betray themselves and harm others cannot be forgiven by history, nor can we compromise with them; what we should guide are general intellectuals, not such people.

Outlying Postal Agency

Changchun Communication, Jilin Province

Small Vendors 176

— Chenxi

The situation in Changchun, in addition to the relatively strong capitalist atmosphere here, is similar to many large cities I have seen in Guannei in some places. All the magnificent appearances that large cities have are also available here, and the most surprising thing is the large number of opium dens and smokers everywhere.

It is said that there are more than 50 opium dens here, and no less than hundreds of thousands of people rely on them directly or indirectly to make a living; in addition, there are more than 100 "small vendors" attached to the front of the opium dens. Although opium is also "banned through taxation" here and has a special sales office, it is not easy for an outsider who has just arrived here to eat it: eating opium here has a certain occasion, similar to the "Yu Li" in Shanghai, and strangers cannot inquire about it.

Opening an opium den here also requires a lot of expenses, just like in Shanghai: donations to the Special Sales Office, "black sales" for inspections and detectives, "filial piety" for gangsters and street politicians, and you have to spend money everywhere to make the business smooth and profitable. However, the miscellaneous expenses spent by the opium den owners are not entirely unrecoverable: for example, the general vendors and merchants in the "small vendors" attached to the front of the opium dens are the targets of the opium den owners' money. Speaking of these vendors in the "small vendors," although they themselves do not necessarily smoke opium, they have to rely on "opium smoking" to make a living all day long: because most of the opium smokers who go to the opium dens to smoke have a "口嬌" (jiao: particular about taste) problem, and they like to eat a little bit of fresh things to change their taste, so the general vendors have to pick up a little bit of residue under the opium smokers' lip service.

Although the "small vendor" is small, it is not inferior to a fair: there are exquisite "eight-treasure porridge," "original soup noodles," "delicious wontons," "finely ground almond tea," and also "smoked beef," "夹烫面火烧" (baked wheaten cake filled with hot noodles), "fruit," "candy," "cigarettes," etc., probably dozens of kinds. Just hearing those exquisite terms, we can't help but salivate, let alone those opium smokers who have a "口嬌" problem?

The situation in front of the opium dens is completely different in the morning and afternoon. The patrons of opium smokers from government offices are usually around 8 o'clock. As for those who come successively after 10 o'clock, most of them are gentlemen of the leisurely upper class and business owners. Therefore, the situation in front of the small vendors also differs in the morning and afternoon. Around 10 o'clock, opium smokers consider it to be the dawn of light, and they have their own preferences in the selection of things at this time. Meat and greasy food are of course not suitable for consumption, and noodles with too much soup are a bit bloated; what should be eaten at this time must be exquisite dim sum. Therefore, in front of the "small vendors" in the early morning, you rarely see担挑 (portable stands) of "wontons," "hanging noodles," or even "eight-treasure porridge": but is business cold? No! The "口嬌" opium smokers are the benefactors who support the vendors: "Hey, give me a bowl of almond tea, shopkeeper!" Opium smokers are mostly good at dealing with the world. Even to a vendor, they are willing to speak in a gentle tone. They all have a successful eloquence, which is trained in the high-level talks by the opium lamp, especially for ordinary greetings: "Hey, is the漿 (soybean milk) hot? Bring two fried dough sticks, shopkeeper!" "Yes, you are! The almond tea is here, the漿 is hot, look, the freshly fried dough sticks!" Is the front of the small vendors in the early morning cold? No, it won't be cold. The small vendors do business at the same time as the opium dens; from early morning to dusk, to late at night, opium dens are constantly patronized by opium smokers, and what about the vendors in front of the door? They are also constantly doing business with those general "口嬌" opium smokers. However, with the different times, their food also has to be changed: almond tea, soy milk, these businesses are the busiest in front of the small vendors in the early morning. When the sun rises high, these owners are washing the pots and bowls. Stalls of "sauce meat," "烧饼 (baked sesame flatbread)," "cigarettes," and "fresh fruit" are also preparing to take over. The "口嬌" opium smokers do not eat too much at noon. The five-cent sauce meat is cut into "knife pieces" and the 烧饼 must be freshly baked. Five cents of meat can be sandwiched between two 烧饼. At this time, in front of the small vendors, you can no longer see the steaming漿 stands and almond tea担挑 in the early morning, but the sound of the grinding rod in the baked food shop, the light of the knife cutting sauce meat, and the conversations of pedestrians are intertwined in front of the small vendors with a雑音调 (mixed tone). In addition, with the shouting of the fruit vendors and the paper candy shop owners next to it, the scenery in front of the small vendors at noon also shows that the small vendor industry that has benefited from the light of opium smokers and opium dens is by no means covered in the wave of recession and depression. When the moment of noon has passed, and the sun is gradually a little slanting, the bustling is followed by a deathly silence; at this time, the number of opium smokers in the opium dens has also decreased; the general office workers have to go to work after talking for about an hour because they have official business. Most of those who remain in the opium dens at this time are the idle class and some businessmen; they occupy a few opium beds sporadically, lying down with their eyes squinted, as if they were propping up the scene for the opium dens for two or three hours. At four or five o'clock in the afternoon, the opium dens began to come to the most brilliant stage of their business of the day; the opium smokers who had worked hard during the day were using nightlife to adjust their spirits at this time; the scene in front of the "small vendors" was replaced by a bustling scene again.

"Wontons are boiling!"

"Eight-treasure porridge! Hot!" This knife-like sharp shout penetrates the tired bodies and minds of the opium smokers, and their emotions suddenly resemble learning a strike; just about to step into the opium den, they will immediately slap themselves back, as if remembering something: "Oh! I'm hungry, let's eat something before smoking opium?"

The roar of the vendors is a very powerful hint: opium smokers are never easily let go when they pass in front of them.

Literary Works

Extracting the Ledger (2) 177

— Puyv

"Dare I? Director Bian is very serious about official affairs, and everyone knows he is iron-faced and selfless." He quietly glanced at me twice, and added two sentences: "Yuan Tai feels that the enemy is evading taxes, and he must be dealt with severely. There are also small distilleries that are naughty. It's rare for the director to come out in person, and he must heal them!"

I almost couldn't help laughing. He patted me again and again, making me both satiated and painful, yet comfortable, and uncomfortable, but I loved this kind of taste, and I was happy with him. In fact, this kid has a talking mouth, a clever mind, and a good face. It's just that his heart is too bad: he calculates others. Honestly, if I hadn't been running errands in the official field for a few years, I might still suffer from him! But then again, his bad intentions hit my heart: several times of financial joy were with his help, and several times of stiff things were relied on him to turn around. So I look up to him and took him along again today. Really, although my appearance is great, I have to cherish talents; for example, just now I was annoyed with him, nothing more than deliberately calculating me, in fact, this is also driven by self-esteem, as long as this bit of stupid energy passes, I will not discuss today's problems with him! (To be continued)

The making of "The Loves of Madame Dubarry" 179

Production cost of one million pounds sterling

British London Films, formerly had several famous productions, such as "The Private Life of Henry VIII," "Catherine the Great," and "The Scarlet Pimpernel," when it was shown in China, they were all a sensation. At that time, the company had two giants: one was Alexander Korda. One is L. Toeplitz, but Toeplitz later broke away from London and formed his own Toeplitz Production Company. He was originally a great British millionaire, and there was no problem with his financial situation. His aim is to produce only four or six films a year, but each one is a blockbuster. The first one cost one million pounds to produce "The Loves of Madame Dubarry" (the film has arrived in Shanghai and will be released in Shanghai soon). He specially invited the great director Victor Saville to take on the director's work for this film, and also recruited Hollywood star Kraft Brock and British red star Marlene Carol to play the leading roles in the film. Therefore, after the premiere, it has won excellent reader praise in Europe and the United States, and it is expected that the harvest in Shanghai in the future will not be inferior to a "The Private Life of Henry VIII" and other films, and it is heard that Hollywood's Sheverlay has also been hired by Toeplitz, and the second product is to invite him to play the leading role, which is indeed a good phenomenon on the British silver scene!

The Detective's Filming Record 180

——A Joke on the Set——

The detective Wang Weixin in "Emerald Horse" is very diligent in the case of drug prohibition and is always planning ways to crack it. As long as he gets a clue, he immediately leads the team to set off.

On this day, the detective Wang Weixin found out that there were a large number of drug dealers transporting drugs on the霹天 (Pitian) set of the Star Company, so he hurried with his brothers, armed with weapons, from the dressing room, straight to the photography set. On this day, the reporter happened to be on the scene. The situation of the two sides fighting with weapons, tense and terrifying, how can we not record it.

It is said that the director Xu Xinfu, who instigated the two sides to fight, stood high on the Zhang Fang table and shouted loudly: "Ready! Kill!"

So Lao Wang got on the Public Security Bureau's truck (naturally fake), and the drug transporters also got on the truck carrying drugs. The two sides opened up their horsepower and rushed straight towards each other. The detective saw the drug dealers' car was not far in front of him, and hurriedly stopped the truck horizontally in the center of the road, blocking the drug dealers' way. At the same time, he opened fire. The drug transporters, seeing this situation, were unwilling to show weakness and fired back. So the good show began, the sound of "啪" (pa) rose up, the situation suddenly became tense, and it was chilling. The detective's gun pointed at the drug dealers and prepared to shoot, but he knew that a Miss standing behind a certain drug dealer watching the filming was startled by this situation and ran away, as if a real bullet was about to fall on her, causing everyone to laugh. As a result of this battle, the "Old Gun" was eaten and abandoned the car. Fortunately, the director Xu Xinfu shouted loudly to stop the poor enemy from pursuing, and the good show ended here.

The reporter stepped forward, shook Lao Wang's hand, and praised his wonderful marksmanship. Lao Wang said with some apologies: "Where, where, no one is afraid of my wooden-shell gun!"

"Wasn't the Miss just now made to be frightened by you?"

Lao Wang couldn't help laughing and told me: "The expressions of the visitors to the many photography sets are often more profound than the actors. Their expressions are often more profound than the actors. When the actors laugh in front of the camera, they also laugh. When the actors cry in front of the camera, they also cry. Just now, I noticed your expression, which was more profound than that of the Miss!"

After being said this by him, the reporter became a little embarrassed and slipped out of the photography set without looking back, secretly admiring that the detective was indeed a great detective, not only was his marksmanship wonderful, but also his eyes were quick and his hands were quick, and even the expressions of the visitors could not escape his sharp eyes.
